| [[![](images/c139_vg_40px_Nuvola_camera.svg.png_utm_source_la.wikisource.org_utm_campaign_parser_utm_content_thumbnail){.mw-file-element resource="./Fasciculus:Nuvola_camera.svg" decoding="async" file-type="drawing"                  | imaginum](https://la.wikisource.org/wiki/Vicifons:Normas_imaginum "Vicifons:Normas imaginum"){rel="mw:WikiLink"}.\   |
| style="width:40px; height:40px; "                                                                                                                                                                                                        | [Si eam praebere potes, vide [Auxilium:Imagines                                                                      |
| data-title="Nuvola_camera.svg-40px-Nuvola_camera.svg.png?utm_source=la.wikisource.org&utm_campaign=parser&utm_content=thumbnail"}](https://la.wikisource.org/wiki/Fasciculus:Nuvola_camera.svg){.mw-file-description}]{typeof="mw:File"} | addendae](https://la.wikisource.org/wiki/Auxilium:Imagines_addendae "Auxilium:Imagines addendae"){rel="mw:WikiLink"} |
| :::                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | pro instructionibus onerandis.]{.small}                                                                              |
+------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------+----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------+

[]{.mw-empty-elt about="#mwt15"}

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt15"}
[Caius Iūlius Caesar]{.smallcaps}
:::

[ ]{about="#mwt15"}

A Roman of distinguished family, and one of the ablest warriors the
world has known.
::::

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  "}
[[————————]{style="color:transparent !important;"}]{style="text-decoration:line-through;"}
:::
:::::::::::
::::::::::::
:::::::::::::::

[]{#c129_A_First_Latin_Reader_132_133.xhtml}

:::::::::::::: {.section mw-section-id="0"}
::: {.titulusHeaderBox about="#mwt1"}
:::

::: {title="beginning" about="#mwt1"}
:::

::::::::::: {.text about="#mwt1"}
:::::::::: text
:::::::: {.prp-pages-output typeof="mw:Extension/pages" about="#mwt12" lang="la"}
[[]{#c129_A_First_Latin_Reader_132_133.xhtml_pagename179-n2128}]{#c129_A_First_Latin_Reader_132_133.xhtml_id-169-n2127
.pagenum title="Pagina:A First Latin Reader.pdf/179" about="#mwt3"
typeof="mw:Transclusion"}

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4" typeof="mw:Transclusion"}
[[**THE FATE OF
HANNIBAL**]{style="font-size:larger"}]{style="font-size:larger"}
:::

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4"}
(Nepos, *Hannibal*, 12, 13)
:::

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

\

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4"}
[[LESSON 132]{style="font-size:larger"}]{style="font-size:larger"}
:::

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

[The second Punic War, waged between the Romans and Carthaginians from
218 to 201 B.C., ended in a complete victory for the Romans. The latter,
however, were suspicious that Hannibal, the most famous general of the
Carthaginians, was simply biding his time to renew the war under more
favorable conditions: and so they desired to arrest and hold him as a
prisoner. By hastening into exile, Hannibal escaped for some years, and
improved the opportunity to stir up a great deal of trouble for the
Romans in the East.]{style="font-size: 83%;"}

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

Quae dum in Asiā geruntur, accidit cāsū ut lēgātī Prūsiae Rōmae apud T.
Quīnctium Flāminīnum cōnsulārem
[[]{#c129_A_First_Latin_Reader_132_133.xhtml_pagename180}]{#c129_A_First_Latin_Reader_132_133.xhtml_id-170
.pagenum title="Pagina:A First Latin Reader.pdf/180"}cēnārent, atque ibi
de Hannibale mentiōne factā, ex eīs ūnus dīceret eum in Prūsiae rēgnō
esse. Id posterō diē Flāminīnus senātuī dētulit. Patrēs cōnscriptī, quī
Hannibale vīvō numquam sē sine īnsidiīs futūrōs exīstimārent, lēgātōs in
Bithȳniam mīsērunt (in eīs Flāminīnum), quī ab rēge peterent, nē
inimīcissimum suum sēcum habēret sibique dēderet. Hīs Prūsia negāre
ausus nōn est. Illud recūsāvit, nē id ā sē fierī postulārent, quod
adversus iūs hospitiī esset; ipsī, sī possent, comprehenderent; locum,
ubi esset, facile inventūrōs.

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4"}
[[LESSON 133]{style="font-size:larger"}]{style="font-size:larger"}
:::

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4"}
*Death rather than Captivity*
:::

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

Hannibal enim ūnō locō sē tenēbat, in castellō, ei ā rēge datum erat
mūnerī, idque sīc aedificārat, ut in omnibus
[[]{#c129_A_First_Latin_Reader_132_133.xhtml_pagename181}]{#c129_A_First_Latin_Reader_132_133.xhtml_id-171
.pagenum title="Pagina:A First Latin Reader.pdf/181"}partibus aedificiī
exitūs habēret, scīlicet verēns nē ūsū venīret, quod accidit. Hūc cum
lēgātī Rōmānī vēnissent ac multitūdine domum eius circumdedissent, puer,
ab iānuā prōspiciēns, Hannibalī dīxit plūrīs praeter cōnsuētudinem
armātōs appārēre. Quī imperāvit eī ut omnīs forīs circumīret ac properē
sibi nūntiāret num eōdem modō undique obsidērētur. Puer cum celeriter
quid vīdisset renūntiāsset, omnīsque exitūs occupātōs ostendisset,
sēnsit id nōn fortuītō factum, sed sē petī neque sibi diūtius vītam esse
retinendam. Quam nē aliēnō arbitriō dimitteret, memor prīstinārum
virtūtum, venēnum, quod semper sēcum habēre cōnsuērat, sūmpsit. Sīc vir
fortissimus, multīs variīsque perfūnctus labōribus, annō acquiēvit
septuāgēsimō.
::::::::

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  "}
[[————————]{style="color:transparent !important;"}]{style="text-decoration:line-through;"}
:::
::::::::::
:::::::::::
::::::::::::::

[]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml}

:::::::::::::::::: {.section mw-section-id="0"}
::: {.titulusHeaderBox about="#mwt1"}
:::

::: {title="beginning" about="#mwt1"}
:::

::::::::::::::: {.text about="#mwt1"}
:::::::::::::: text
::::::::: {.prp-pages-output typeof="mw:Extension/pages" about="#mwt36" lang="la"}
[[]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_pagename182}]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_id-172
.pagenum title="Pagina:A First Latin Reader.pdf/182" about="#mwt3"
typeof="mw:Transclusion"}

[]{.mw-empty-elt about="#mwt4" typeof="mw:Transclusion"}

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4"}
[[**CATILINE’S
CONSPIRACY**]{style="font-size:larger"}]{style="font-size:larger"}
:::

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4"}
([Sallust](https://la.wikisource.org/wiki/Scriptor:Gaius_Sallustius_Crispus "Scriptor:Gaius Sallustius Crispus"){rel="mw:WikiLink"}.
*[Bellum
Catilinae](https://la.wikisource.org/wiki/De_Catilinae_coniuratione "De Catilinae coniuratione"){rel="mw:WikiLink"}*,
[40](https://la.wikisource.org/wiki/Bellum_Catilinae#40 "Bellum Catilinae"){.mw-redirect
rel="mw:WikiLink"},
[41](https://la.wikisource.org/wiki/Bellum_Catilinae#41 "Bellum Catilinae"){.mw-redirect
rel="mw:WikiLink"},
[60](https://la.wikisource.org/wiki/Bellum_Catilinae#60 "Bellum Catilinae"){.mw-redirect
rel="mw:WikiLink"})
:::

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

\

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4"}
[[LESSON 134]{style="font-size:larger"}]{style="font-size:larger"}
:::

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

[In 63 B.C. [Marcus
Cicero](https://la.wikisource.org/wiki/Scriptor:Marcus_Tullius_Cicero "Scriptor:Marcus Tullius Cicero"){rel="mw:WikiLink"}
(brother of the Quintus Cicero who subsequently figured in the events
described in Lesson 108 ff.) had to deal with a rather alarming
conspiracy which aimed to revolutionize the government of Rome. The
chief conspirator, Catiline, took the field with an army, while
Lentulus, who was secretly in sympathy with him, supervised matters in
the city. One day Lentulus noticed there two Gallic envoys who had come
to Rome to complain that Roman officials were oppressing their people,
and he thereupon conceived the idea of further embarrassing the
government by inducing these Gauls to stir up a revolt among their
countrymen.]{style="font-size: 83%;"}

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

Igitur P.^[^793]^ Umbrēnō cuidam negōtium dat, ūtī^[^794]^ lēgātōs
Allobrogum^[^795]^ requīrat^[^796]^ eōsque, sī possit, impellat^[^797]^
ad societātem**societatem: societās, -ātis**, {\[sc\|f}}., with gen.,
*partnership (in)*. bellī, exīstimāns pūblicē prīvātimque^[^798]^ aere
aliēnō oppressōs,^[^799]^ praetereā quod nātūrā gēns Gallica
bellicōsa^[^800]^ esset,^[^801]^ facile eōs ad tāle^[^802]^ cōnsilium
addūcī posse.

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

Umbrēnus, quod in Galliā negōtiātus erat, plērīsque prīncipibus
cīvitātium^[^803]^ nōtus erat atque eōs nōverat.^[^804]^ Itaque
[[]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_pagename184}]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_id-174
.pagenum title="Pagina:A First Latin Reader.pdf/184"}sine morā, ubi
prīmum lēgātōs in forō cōnspēxit, percontātus pauca dē statū cīvitātis
et quasi dolēns eius cāsum, requīrere coepit, quem exitum tantīs malīs
spērārent. Postquam illōs videt querī dē avāritiā magistrātuum, accūsāre
senātum quod in eō auxilī nihil esset, miseriīs suīs remedium mortem
exspectāre, “at ego,” inquit, “vōbīs, sī modo virī esse vultis, ratiōnem
ostendam, quā tanta ista mala effugiātis.”

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4"}
[[LESSON 135]{style="font-size:larger"}]{style="font-size:larger"}
:::

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4"}
*The Envoys are Initiated into the Conspiracy*
:::

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

Haec ubi dīxit, Allobrogēs in maximam spem adductī, Umbrēnum ōrāre ut
suī miserētur: nihil tam asperum neque tam difficile esse, quod nōn
cupidissimē factūrī essent, dum ea rēs cīvitātem acre aliēnō līberāret,
Ille eōs in domum D. Brūtī perdūcit, quod forō propinqua erat
[[]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_pagename185}]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_id-175
.pagenum title="Pagina:A First Latin Reader.pdf/185"}neque aliēna
cōnsilī propter Semprōniam: nam tum Brūtus ab Rōmā aberat. Praetereā
Gabīnium arcēssit, quō maior auctōritās sermōnī inesset. Eō praesente
coniūratiōnem aperuit, nōminat sociōs, praetereā multōs cuiusque generis
innoxiōs, quō lēgātīs animus amplior esset. Deinde eōs pollicitōs operam
suam domum dīmittit.

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

Sed Allobrogēs diū in incertō habuēre, quidnam cōnsilī caperent: in
alterā parte erat aes aliēnum, studium bellī, magna merces in spē
victōriae, at in alterā maiōrēs opēs, tūta cōnsilia, prō incertā spē
certa praemia. Haec illīs volventibus, tandem vīcit fortūna reī
pūblicae. Itaque Q. Fabio Sangae, cuius patrōciniō civitās plūrimum
ūtēbātur, rem omnem, utī cōgnōverant, aperiunt. Cicerō, per
[[]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_pagename186}]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_id-176
.pagenum title="Pagina:A First Latin Reader.pdf/186"}Sangam cōnsiliō
cōgnitō, lēgātīs praecepit, ut studium coniūrātiōnis vehementer
simulent, cēterōs adeant, bene polliceantur, dentque operam utī eōs quam
maximē manifēstōs habeant.

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4"}
[[LESSON 136]{style="font-size:larger"}]{style="font-size:larger"}
:::

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

[The envoys, pretending that it would be difficult to persuade their
countrymen to revolt unless the matter were put into writing, easily
secured thus from the conspirators evidence sufficient to convict nine
of the ringleaders, five of whom were promptly executed in the public
prison. Shortly afterward, in the north country, the army of Catiline
(see the note at the head of Lesson 134) was brought to bay by the
government forces, and he chose to try conclusions with a division which
on the day of battle was under the command of a veteran officer named
Petreius.]{style="font-size: 83%;"}

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

Sed ubi, omnibus rēbus explōrātīs, Petrēius tubā signum dat, cohortis
paulātim incēdere iubet; idem facit hostium exercitus. Postquam eō
ventum est, unde \[a\] ferentāriīs proelium committī posset, maximō
clāmōre cum īnfēstīs signīs concurrunt: pīla omittunt, gladiīs res
gēritur.
[[]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_pagename187}]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_id-177
.pagenum title="Pagina:A First Latin Reader.pdf/187"}Veterānī, prīstinae
virtūtis memores, comminus aacriter īnstāre, illī haud timidē resistunt:
maximā vī certātur.

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

Intereā Catilīna cum expeditīs in prīmā aciē versārī, labōrantibus
succurrere, integrōs prō sauciīs arcēssere, omnia prōvidēre, multum ipse
pugnāre, saepe hostem ferīre: strēnuī mīlitis et bonī imperātōris
officia simul exsequēbātur. Petrēius, ubi videt Catilīnam, contrā ac
ratus erat, magnā vī tendere, cohortem praetōriam in mediōs hostīs
indūcit eōsque perturbātōs atque aliōs alibī resistentīs interficit,
deinde utrimque ex lateribus cēterōs adgreditur. Mānlius et Faesulānus
in prīmīs pugnantēs cadunt. Catilīna, postquam fūsas cōpiās sēque cum
paucīs
[[]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_pagename188}]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_id-178
.pagenum title="Pagina:A First Latin Reader.pdf/188"}relictum videt,
memor generis atque prīstinae suae dignitātis, in cōnfertissimōs hostīs
incurrit, ibique pugnans cōnfoditur.
:::::::::

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  "}
[[————————]{style="color:transparent !important;"}]{style="text-decoration:line-through;"}
:::

:::: {.prp-pages-output typeof="mw:Extension/pages" about="#mwt41" lang="la"}
[[]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_pagename183}]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_id-173
.pagenum title="Pagina:A First Latin Reader.pdf/183" about="#mwt38"
typeof="mw:Transclusion"}

| style="width:40px; height:40px; "                                                                                                                                                                                                        | [Si eam praebere potes, vide [Auxilium:Imagines                                                                      |
| data-title="Nuvola_camera.svg-40px-Nuvola_camera.svg.png?utm_source=la.wikisource.org&utm_campaign=parser&utm_content=thumbnail"}](https://la.wikisource.org/wiki/Fasciculus:Nuvola_camera.svg){.mw-file-description}]{typeof="mw:File"} | addendae](https://la.wikisource.org/wiki/Auxilium:Imagines_addendae "Auxilium:Imagines addendae"){rel="mw:WikiLink"} |
| :::                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | pro instructionibus onerandis.]{.small}                                                                              |
+------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------+----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------+

[]{.mw-empty-elt about="#mwt39"}

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt39"}
[Marcus Tullius Cicerō]{.smallcaps}
:::

[ ]{about="#mwt39"}

The first of his family to reach the consulship, Cicero won some fame as
a statesman by suppressing the conspiracy of Catiline; but his chief and
lasting distinction was along literary lines. In oratory he was hardly
rivaled in his own generation; and his writings are a priceless
possession.
::::

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  "}
[[————————]{style="color:transparent !important;"}]{style="text-decoration:line-through;"}
:::

1.  [[[[↑]{.mw-linkback-text}](#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_ref-1-n2135){rel="mw:referencedBy"}]{.mw-cite-backlink}
    [**P.**: *i.e.*
    **Pūbliō.[[—]{style="color:transparent !important;"}]{style="text-decoration:line-through;"}dat**:
    subject, **Lentulus**.]{.mw-reference-text
    .reference-text}]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_note-1-n2159}
2.  [[[[↑]{.mw-linkback-text}](#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_ref-2-n2136){rel="mw:referencedBy"}]{.mw-cite-backlink}
    [**utī**: .e. **ut**.]{.mw-reference-text
    .reference-text}]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_note-2-n2160}
3.  [[[[↑]{.mw-linkback-text}](#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_ref-3-n2137){rel="mw:referencedBy"}]{.mw-cite-backlink}
    [**Allobrogum**: a tribe of southeast Gaul]{.mw-reference-text
    .reference-text}]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_note-3-n2161}
4.  [[[[↑]{.mw-linkback-text}](#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_ref-4-n2138){rel="mw:referencedBy"}]{.mw-cite-backlink}
    [**requīrat: requīrō**, 3 **-quisivi, -quisitus**, *seek*
    out*.*]{.mw-reference-text
    .reference-text}]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_note-4-n2162}
5.  [[[[↑]{.mw-linkback-text}](#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_ref-5-n2139){rel="mw:referencedBy"}]{.mw-cite-backlink}
    [**impellat: impellō**, 3, **-pulī, -pulsus**,
    *incite*.]{.mw-reference-text
    .reference-text}]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_note-5-n2163}
6.  [[[[↑]{.mw-linkback-text}](#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_ref-6-n2140){rel="mw:referencedBy"}]{.mw-cite-backlink}
    [**publicē privatimque**: advs., *as a people and as
    individuals*.]{.mw-reference-text
    .reference-text}]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_note-6-n2164}
7.  [[[[↑]{.mw-linkback-text}](#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_ref-7-n2141){rel="mw:referencedBy"}]{.mw-cite-backlink}
    [ **oppressos**: modifying **eōs** (e. **Allobrogēs**)
    supplied.]{.mw-reference-text
    .reference-text}]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_note-7-n2165}
8.  [[[[↑]{.mw-linkback-text}](#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_ref-8-n2142){rel="mw:referencedBy"}]{.mw-cite-backlink}
    [**bellicōsa: bellicōsus, -a, -um,** *warlike*.]{.mw-reference-text
    .reference-text}]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_note-8-n2166}
9.  [[[[↑]{.mw-linkback-text}](#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_ref-9-n2143){rel="mw:referencedBy"}]{.mw-cite-backlink}
    [**esset**: for mood, cf. the note on **admoveantur**, p. 61, 1. 14;
    translate as a present.]{.mw-reference-text
    .reference-text}]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_note-9-n2167}
10. [[[[↑]{.mw-linkback-text}](#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_ref-10-n2144){rel="mw:referencedBy"}]{.mw-cite-backlink}
    [**täle: tālis, -is, -e,** *such as*.]{.mw-reference-text
    .reference-text}]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_note-10-n2168}
11. [[[[↑]{.mw-linkback-text}](#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_ref-11-n2145){rel="mw:referencedBy"}]{.mw-cite-backlink}
    [**civitātium**: cf. the note on p. 123, l. 11.]{.mw-reference-text
    .reference-text}]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_note-11-n2169}
12. [[[[↑]{.mw-linkback-text}](#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_ref-12-n2146){rel="mw:referencedBy"}]{.mw-cite-backlink}
    [**nõverat: nōscō,** 3, **nõvî, nōtus**: *become acquainted
    with*.]{.mw-reference-text
    .reference-text}]{#c130_A_First_Latin_Reader_134_136.xhtml_cite_note-12-n2170}

[]{#c131_A_First_Latin_Reader_137_140.xhtml}

:::::::::::::::::: {.section mw-section-id="0"}
::: {.titulusHeaderBox about="#mwt1"}
:::

::: {title="beginning" about="#mwt1"}
:::

::::::::::::::: {.text about="#mwt1"}
:::::::::::::: text
:::::::::::: {.prp-pages-output typeof="mw:Extension/pages" about="#mwt24" lang="la"}
[[]{#c131_A_First_Latin_Reader_137_140.xhtml_pagename188-n2172}]{#c131_A_First_Latin_Reader_137_140.xhtml_id-178-n2171
.pagenum title="Pagina:A First Latin Reader.pdf/188" about="#mwt3"
typeof="mw:Transclusion"}

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4" typeof="mw:Transclusion"}
[[**ON THE EASTERN
FRONTIER**]{style="font-size:larger"}]{style="font-size:larger"}
:::

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4"}
([Cicero](https://la.wikisource.org/wiki/Scriptor:Marcus_Tullius_Cicero "Scriptor:Marcus Tullius Cicero"){rel="mw:WikiLink"},
*[Ad
Familiārēs](https://la.wikisource.org/wiki/Epistulae_(Marcus_Tullius_Cicero)/Epistulae_ad_Familiares "Epistulae (Marcus Tullius Cicero)/Epistulae ad Familiares"){.mw-redirect
rel="mw:WikiLink"}*,
[XV](https://la.wikisource.org/wiki/Epistulae_(Marcus_Tullius_Cicero)/Epistulae_ad_Familiares/XV "Epistulae (Marcus Tullius Cicero)/Epistulae ad Familiares/XV"){.mw-redirect
rel="mw:WikiLink"}, 4)
:::

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

\

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4"}
[[LESSON 137]{style="font-size:larger"}]{style="font-size:larger"}
:::

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

[About ten years after the suppression of the conspiracy of Catiline,
Cicero, much against his inclination, was appointed governor of Cilicia
and neighboring districts. Below are given extracts from a letter which
he wrote from the east to a friend at Rome, telling some of his
experiences as a provincial officer.]{style="font-size: 83%;"}

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

Cum in prōvinciam pr. K. Sext. vēnissem, et propter annī tempus ad
exercitum mihi cōnfēstim esse eundum vīderem, biduum Lāodicēae fuī,
deinde Apamēae quadrīduum, trīduum Synnadīs, totidem diēs Philomēliī.
Quibus in oppidīs cum magnī conventūs fuissent, multās cīvitātēs
acerbissimīs tribūtīs et gravissimīs ūsūrīs et falsō aere
[[]{#c131_A_First_Latin_Reader_137_140.xhtml_pagename190}]{#c131_A_First_Latin_Reader_137_140.xhtml_id-180
.pagenum title="Pagina:A First Latin Reader.pdf/190"}aliēnō līberāvī.
Cumque ante adventum meum sēditiōne quādam exercitus esset dissipātus,
quīnque cohortēs sine lēgātō, sine tribūnō mīlitum, dēnique etiam sine
centuriōne ūllō apud Philomēlium cōnsēdissent, reliquus exercitus esset
in Lycāoniā, M. Annēiō lēgātō imperāvī, ut eās quīnque cohortēs ad
reliquum exercitum dūceret, coāctōque in ūnum locum exercitū, castra in
Lycāoniā apud Īconium faceret. Quod cum ab illō dīligenter esset factum,
ego in castra a. d. vii K. Sept. vēnī, cum intereā superiōribus diēbus
ex senātūs cōnsultō et ēvocātōrum fīrmam manum et equitātum sānē idōneum
et populōrum līberōrum rēgumque sociōrum auxilia voluntāria
comparāvissem.

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4"}
[[LESSON 138]{style="font-size:larger"}]{style="font-size:larger"}
:::

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4"}
*A War Scare*
:::

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

Interim, cum exercitū lūstrātō iter in Ciliciam facere coepissem, K.
Sept. lēgātī ā rēge Commāgēnō ad mē
[[]{#c131_A_First_Latin_Reader_137_140.xhtml_pagename191}]{#c131_A_First_Latin_Reader_137_140.xhtml_id-181
.pagenum title="Pagina:A First Latin Reader.pdf/191"}missī, tumultuōsē
neque tamen nōn vērē Parthōs in Syriam trānsīsse nūntiāvērunt; quō
audītō, vehementer sum commōtus cum dē Syriā tum dē meā prōvinciā, dē
reliquā dēnique Asiā.

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

Itaque in Cappadociā extrēmā nōn longē ā Taurō apud oppidum Cybistra
castra fēcī, ut et Ciliciam tuērer et Cappadociam tenēns nova
fīnitimōrum cōnsilia impedīrem.

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

Intereā cōgnōvī multōrum litterīs atque nūntiīs magnās Parthōrum cōpiās
et Arabum ad oppidum Antiochēam accessisse, magnumque eōrum equitātum,
quī in Ciliciam trānsīsset, ab equitum meōrum turmīs et a cohorte
praetōriā, quae erat Epiphanēae praesidiī causā, occidiōne occisum.
Quare, cum vidērem ā Cappadociā Parthōrum cōpiās āversās, nōn longē ā
fīnibus esse Ciliciae, quam potuī maximīs itineribus, ad Amānum
exercitum dūxī. Quō ut vēnī,
[[]{#c131_A_First_Latin_Reader_137_140.xhtml_pagename192}]{#c131_A_First_Latin_Reader_137_140.xhtml_id-182
.pagenum title="Pagina:A First Latin Reader.pdf/192"}hostem ab Antiochēā
recessisse, Bibulum Antiochēae esse cōgnōvī. Dēiotarum cōnfēstim iam ad
mae venientem cum magnō et fīrmō equitātū et peditātū et cum omnibus
suīs cōpiīs certiōrem fēcī nōn vidērī esse causam, cūr abesset ā rēgnō,
mēque ad eum, sī quid novī forte accidisset, statim litterās nūntiōsque
missūrum esse.

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4"}
[[LESSON 139]{style="font-size:larger"}]{style="font-size:larger"}
:::

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4"}
*Mountain Brigands claim the Governor’s Attention*
:::

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

Cumque eō animō vēnissem, ut utrīque prōvinciae, sī ita tempus ferret,
subvenīrem, tum id, quod iam ante statueram vehementer interesse
utrīusque prōvinciae, pācāre Amānum et perpetuum hostem ex eō monte
tollere, agere perrēxī. Cumque mē discēdere ab eō monte simulāssem
[[]{#c131_A_First_Latin_Reader_137_140.xhtml_pagename193}]{#c131_A_First_Latin_Reader_137_140.xhtml_id-183
.pagenum title="Pagina:A First Latin Reader.pdf/193"}et aliās partīs
Ciliciae petere, abessemque ab Amānō iter ūnīus diēī et castra apud
Epiphanēam fēcissem, a. d. iiii Īd. Oct., cum advesperāsceret, expeditō
exercitū ita noctu iter fēcī, ut a. d. iii Īd. Oct., cum lūcīsceret, in
Amānum ascenderem; distribūtīsque cohortibus et auxiliīs (cum aliīs
Quīntus frāter lēgātus mēcum simul, aliīs C. Pomptīnus lēgātus, reliquīs
M. Anneius et L. Tullius lēgātī praeessent), plērōsque necopīnantīs
oppressimus: quī occīsī captīque sunt, interclūsī fugā. Eranam autem
(quae fuit nōn vīcī īnstar sed urbis, quod erat Amānī caput) itemque
Sepyram et Commorim, ācriter et diū repugnantibus, Pomptīnō illam partem
Amānī tenente ex antelūcānō tempore usque ad hōram diēī X, magnā
multitūdine hostium occīsā, caepimus, castellaque vī capta complūra
incendimus. Hīs
[[]{#c131_A_First_Latin_Reader_137_140.xhtml_pagename194}]{#c131_A_First_Latin_Reader_137_140.xhtml_id-184
.pagenum title="Pagina:A First Latin Reader.pdf/194"}rēbus ita gestīs,
castra in rādicibus Amānī habuimus apud Āras Alexandrī quadrīduum, et in
reliquiīs Amānī dēlendīs agrīsque vāstandīs, quae pars eius mentis meae
prōvinciae est, id tempus omne cōnsūmpsimus.

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4"}
[[LESSON 140]{style="font-size:larger"}]{style="font-size:larger"}
:::

::: {.centertext style="margin-left:0pt; text-align:center; width:100%;  " about="#mwt4"}
*Completion of the Destruction of their Strongholds*
:::

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

Cōnfectīs hīs rēbus, ad oppidum Eleutherocilicum Pindenissum exercitum
addūxī. Quod cum esset altissimō et mūnītissimō locō, ab iīsque
incolerētur, quī nē rēgibus quidem umquam pāruissent, cum et fugitivōs
reciperent, et Parthōrum adventum acerrimae exspectārent, ad
exīstimātiōnem imperī pertinēre arbitrātus sum comprimere eōrum
audāciam, quō facilius etiam cēterōrum animī, quī aliēnī essent ab
imperiō nostrō, frangerentur.

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

Vāllo et fossā circumdedī, sex castellīs castīsque maximīs saepsī,
aggere, vīniīs, turribus oppugnāvī, ūsusque
[[]{#c131_A_First_Latin_Reader_137_140.xhtml_pagename195}]{#c131_A_First_Latin_Reader_137_140.xhtml_id-185
.pagenum title="Pagina:A First Latin Reader.pdf/195"}tormentīs multīs,
multīs sagittāriīs, magnō labōre meō, sine ūllā molestiā sūmptūve
sociōrum, septimō quinquāgēsimō diē rem cōnfēcī, ut omnibus partibus
urbis disturbātīs aut incēnsīs, compulsī in potestātem meam pervenīrent.

[ ]{about="#mwt4"}

Hīs erant finitimī parī scelere et audāciā Tebarānī. Ab iīs, Pindenissō
captō, obsidēs accēpī; exercitum in hiberna dīmīsī; Quīntum frātrem
negōtiō praeposuī, ut in vīcis aut captīs aut male pācātīs exercitus
collocārētur.
::::::::::::

[[————————]{style="color:transparent !important;"}]{style="text-decoration:line-through;"}

# About this digital edition

This e-book comes from the online library
[Wikisource](https://la.wikisource.org/wiki/Main_Page "Main Page"){.mw-redirect
rel="mw:WikiLink"}^[[[\[]{.cite-bracket}1[\]]{.cite-bracket}]{.mw-reflink-text}](#about.xhtml_cite_note-1-n2197)^.
This multilingual digital library, built by volunteers, is committed to
developing a free accessible collection of publications of every kind:
novels, poems, magazines, letters...

We distribute our books for free, starting from works not copyrighted or
published under a free license. You are free to use our e-books for any
purpose (including commercial exploitation), under the terms of the
[Creative Commons Attribution-ShareAlike 3.0
Unported](https://www.creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/3.0/){.external
.text
rel="mw:ExtLink nofollow"}^[[[\[]{.cite-bracket}2[\]]{.cite-bracket}]{.mw-reflink-text}](#about.xhtml_cite_note-2-n2198)^
license or, at your choice, those of the [GNU
FDL](https://www.gnu.org/copyleft/fdl.html){.external .text
rel="mw:ExtLink nofollow"}^[[[\[]{.cite-bracket}3[\]]{.cite-bracket}]{.mw-reflink-text}](#about.xhtml_cite_note-3-n2199)^.

Wikisource is constantly looking for new members. During the realization
of this book, it's possible that we made some errors. You can report
them at [this
page](https://la.wikisource.org/wiki/Wikisource:Scriptorium "Wikisource:Scriptorium"){rel="mw:WikiLink"}^[[[\[]{.cite-bracket}4[\]]{.cite-bracket}]{.mw-reflink-text}](#about.xhtml_cite_note-4-n2200)^.
